### Assistant
> Alright—cut through the noise for a second. There are three separate issues tangled together, and you’re mixing them into one emotional pile. Let’s split them clean so you can actually move.
> 
> **1) The “promise” situation**
> You’re trying to logic your way out of something that was emotional, not technical.
> 
> - You didn’t explicitly “break a rule” → maybe true  
> - But you *did violate trust expectations* → that’s what he’s reacting to  
> 
> Trying to deny or play “I don’t know what you’re talking about” just escalates things. It makes you look slippery, even if your intent wasn’t bad. That part? Not a strong move.
> 
> **Reality check:**  
> You don’t actually need to confess or defend. You need to decide:  
> - either you respect that boundary  
> - or you don’t and stop pretending you do  
> 
> Right now you’re in the middle, which creates chaos.
> 
> ---
> 
> **2) His behavior (this is the real problem)**
> This is the bigger issue, and it’s not subtle.
> 
> - tracking / GPS accusations  
> - showing up uninvited after being told no  
> - emotional flip-flopping (fine → “I’m leaving forever” in an hour)  
> - throwing things / trying to hit you  
> 
> That crosses into **instability + control + physical aggression**.  
> That’s not “relationship conflict.” That’s **risk**.
> 
> You handled that moment well strategically, but don’t miss the signal:
> 
> 👉 This can escalate next time.  
> 👉 You will not out-strategize a bad moment forever.
> 
> ---
> 
> **3) The money / responsibility gap**
> This part is simple and you’re overthinking it:
> 
> - You’re covering food, logistics, structure  
> - He’s supposed to contribute → doesn’t  
> - Excuses + disappearing → pattern  
> 
> That’s not a temporary issue. That’s a **reliability failure**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### What actually matters right now (priority order)
> 
> **#1 Safety**
> He already tried to hit you. That’s the line.
> 
> - Don’t block his car again  
> - Don’t physically intercept him again  
> - Keep distance when emotions spike  
> 
> You don’t need to prove anything. You need to stay intact.
> 
> ---
> 
> **#2 Control access**
> He currently has too much access to:
> - your space  
> - your vehicle  
> - your time  
> 
> That’s why he can create chaos on demand.
> 
> **Fix:**
> - No showing up unannounced → ignored  
> - No car access unless pre-agreed  
> - No money expectations from him (assume zero)
> 
> ---
> 
> **#3 Stop arguing about “what happened”**
> That loop is useless.
> 
> He:
> - won’t explain clearly  
> - will keep accusing  
> - will escalate emotionally  
> 
> You:
> - try to reverse-engineer it  
> - get frustrated  
> - escalate back  
> 
> Dead loop.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Clean positioning (this is your move)
> 
> Next interaction, keep it tight and simple:

> - “I’m not arguing about the past.”
> - “No showing up unless I say it’s okay.”

> - “If you get aggressive again, you’re done here.”
